        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393770910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17839823363071807027">The word c**t and completely emotionless/hate-filled sex plus casual drug use does not make a story either good, controversial or interesting. There feels like there is only one character in this book, but it assumes different ancestry and genders. Just one hate-filled, drug and alcohol-fuelled zombie, playing all the parts. I hate this book, hate it, hate it, hate it, if I could unwrite it, I would. Books don't have to be angel sparkles, ginger beer and licky happy dogs, I don't mind anger/hate</span>
  <span id="freeText17839823363071807027" style="display:none">The word c**t and completely emotionless/hate-filled sex plus casual drug use does not make a story either good, controversial or interesting. There feels like there is only one character in this book, but it assumes different ancestry and genders. Just one hate-filled, drug and alcohol-fuelled zombie, playing all the parts. I hate this book, hate it, hate it, hate it, if I could unwrite it, I would. Books don't have to be angel sparkles, ginger beer and licky happy dogs, I don't mind anger/hate/ennui in books, in fact, I don't even need to like the characters but this book has no redeeming features; the writing is uninventive, the characters one-dimensional and that dimension is hateful, the dialogue forced, the characters without direction, the story rambly etc etc. <br /><br />Despite all of this, I'd still not rate it so badly if I felt there was a point, even if that point was just to reflect a section of society, but NO ONE thinks like this. Or at least, no large group of people are such an accumulated pack of wankers, I refuse to believe it.<br /><br />It's not so bad it's good, it's just really really really bad. Please don't read it. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=overhyped">overhyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135802709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18234225492748737715">The Slap wasn't really anything like I was expected. From the title and the description, I expected the plot to be focused around the aftermath of Harry slapping his friends' child. Instead, it really just focused around the relationships of all the acquaintances and their personal lives. The Slap was mentioned a few times throughout the book but it really felt like it was in the background. I found it very hard to like any of the character as they were all incredibly selfish and hate-filled but</span>
  <span id="freeText18234225492748737715" style="display:none">The Slap wasn't really anything like I was expected. From the title and the description, I expected the plot to be focused around the aftermath of Harry slapping his friends' child. Instead, it really just focused around the relationships of all the acquaintances and their personal lives. The Slap was mentioned a few times throughout the book but it really felt like it was in the background. I found it very hard to like any of the character as they were all incredibly selfish and hate-filled but at the same time, I did find them interesting to read about. They were all living double lives basically and all secretly disliked each other. The book wasn't what I thought it would be and it wasn't amazing but it was still interesting and I was not bored at any point. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18234225492748737715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1475568020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1475568020" />
    <a title="Licha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5614272-licha"><img alt="Licha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337135662p2/5614272.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1475568020?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Licha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Licha" href="/user/show/5614272-licha">Licha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143117148" href="/book/show/6632916-the-slap">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1475568020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2494254552916502833">Hated this book. Really hated ALL the characters in this book. I'm probably being a little too harsh to give this one star since I somehow managed to finish the book. The subject was interesting, but I just didn't like it.<br/><br/>The author seemed like he wanted to push every button he could and go extreme with it. The book touches on racism to the point where it's cringe worthy, using every kind of racist comment or stereotype it can. It's very misogynistic, making every man in the story come off as so</span>
  <span id="freeText2494254552916502833" style="display:none">Hated this book. Really hated ALL the characters in this book. I'm probably being a little too harsh to give this one star since I somehow managed to finish the book. The subject was interesting, but I just didn't like it.<br /><br />The author seemed like he wanted to push every button he could and go extreme with it. The book touches on racism to the point where it's cringe worthy, using every kind of racist comment or stereotype it can. It's very misogynistic, making every man in the story come off as some kind of a-hole. I would hate to run into any of the men in this story. <br /><br />The story begins at a barbecue where a group of friends and family are gathered. We are introduced to Hugo, the worst bratty little three year old kid you could ever meet. After several little antics Hugo has at the party, one father finally has had enough and impulsively slaps Hugo in the face. This sets off what happens next in the book, which is not always about the slap. We get too much background on these people as each tells his version and story in relation to the other characters. Just when you think you're finally coming across a character that might just be ok, they do or say something despicable. Every single character was the type of person you would not want to be friends with. And every chapter has to bring some kind of icky sex scene to the table. In Rosie's (Hugo's mom, an extremely, I mean extremely, dislikable woman) chapter there's a scene where Hugo and dad compete for her breast. Yes, this is a three year old who gets breastfed at the drop of a hat, anywhere and in front of anyone. This makes every one in the story uncomfortable and no doubtedly plays into their dislike for Hugo. Both dad and Hugo play tug-o-war with Rosie's breast, each claiming, 'No mine.' 'No, mine", back and forth. <br /><br />There's a scene where one of the teenage boys is going to go to a party. His mom asks him if he's going to take any drugs at the party. The boy (Richie) tells her it is more than likely he will. She replies, "Oh baby. I guess you're all grown up." What!? <br /><br />I just couldn't get with any of these characters or the way the slap was handled by all the characters as each is forced to take sides. A very uncomfortable read, for sure.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2494254552916502833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17973812554944566164">A group of people are gathered at a suburban Barbecue. During the afternoon an incident between one of the guests and a four year old result in consequences that directly, or indirectly, affect all who are present.<br/><br/>Told as a collection of short stories through the perspective of eight characters, all with different background, age, ethnicity and value systems, The Slap is a provocative, unflinching novel that explores our inner most beliefs and the conflicting issues we face. I enjoyed having a d</span>
  <span id="freeText17973812554944566164" style="display:none">A group of people are gathered at a suburban Barbecue. During the afternoon an incident between one of the guests and a four year old result in consequences that directly, or indirectly, affect all who are present.<br /><br />Told as a collection of short stories through the perspective of eight characters, all with different background, age, ethnicity and value systems, The Slap is a provocative, unflinching novel that explores our inner most beliefs and the conflicting issues we face. I enjoyed having a different portal in which the same situation has been explored. Hearing the different points of view shows there is no black or white situation - that our beliefs are a sum of all our life's experiences.<br /><br />The Slap is hands down my clear favourite amongst this year's Australian fiction and if there is any justice in the world, the judges of The Booker &amp; The Miles Franklin Award will agree. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11594919123443926042">I’m probably one of the few people in my group of friends that actually finished this book. I don’t think I have ever read a book that has left me with such raw and mixed emotions before. I was totally drained! There were at times when I wanted to fling the book against the wall in utter disgust and there were others where I felt such sympathy for the characters inner turmoil that I wanted to embraces them and tell them it was all okay. This was a very hard book to read. But the thing I really l</span>
  <span id="freeText11594919123443926042" style="display:none">I’m probably one of the few people in my group of friends that actually finished this book. I don’t think I have ever read a book that has left me with such raw and mixed emotions before. I was totally drained! There were at times when I wanted to fling the book against the wall in utter disgust and there were others where I felt such sympathy for the characters inner turmoil that I wanted to embraces them and tell them it was all okay. This was a very hard book to read. But the thing I really loved about it is how it affected me in this way. Very clever and powerful piece of writing.</span>

    <a title="H.A. Leuschel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56337479-h-a-leuschel"><img alt="H.A. Leuschel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496742235p2/56337479.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2404151959?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="H.A. Leuschel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="H.A. Leuschel" href="/user/show/56337479-h-a-leuschel">H.A. Leuschel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848873568" href="/book/show/10077148-the-slap">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2404151959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11642725947513222236">This is a thought-provoking, bold and gripping read. The characters were challenging and multi-faceted because as the story progressed revelations about their past would make them appear in a different light and the motive of their actions would also alter the reader's views about them. The descriptions of graphic sex scenes and an overuse of swear words spoiled it for me at times as I cringed or flinched trying to wade through explicit sections which in my view were not necessary and the crude </span>
  <span id="freeText11642725947513222236" style="display:none">This is a thought-provoking, bold and gripping read. The characters were challenging and multi-faceted because as the story progressed revelations about their past would make them appear in a different light and the motive of their actions would also alter the reader's views about them. The descriptions of graphic sex scenes and an overuse of swear words spoiled it for me at times as I cringed or flinched trying to wade through explicit sections which in my view were not necessary and the crude language overly provocative. The book's main premise though - a BBQ where an adult slaps another person's young son - is a great idea for how an event can ripple through a group of friends and bring out their hidden animosities, their views on education and ultimately what they believe is the basis of moral behaviour. It's a book that made me think and I think would make good bookclub material!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11642725947513222236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3011905690" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11315868270189164770">The cover asks ‘whose side are you on’ and having finished it I found that no one involved in this plot is either fully justified or blameless.<br/><br/>The split narratives offered such a variety of perspectives and points of empathy that I found it a pretty thought provoking text in terms of my own initial judgements. That said, I do wish there had been a bit more of a ‘comeuppance’ for some of the characters (although I’ll admit this could have resulted in an ultra-cheesy, justice-laden ending). Manoli</span>
  <span id="freeText11315868270189164770" style="display:none">The cover asks ‘whose side are you on’ and having finished it I found that no one involved in this plot is either fully justified or blameless.<br /><br />The split narratives offered such a variety of perspectives and points of empathy that I found it a pretty thought provoking text in terms of my own initial judgements. That said, I do wish there had been a bit more of a ‘comeuppance’ for some of the characters (although I’ll admit this could have resulted in an ultra-cheesy, justice-laden ending). Manolis’s section, that dealt beautifully with themes of loss and societal change, was the one I enjoyed reading the most, but I loved the feeling of shifting to a new character perspective throughout. This was recommended to me by a fellow goodreader (having never read Tsiolkas before) and I’m now keen to read more.<br /><br />There was only one small negative worth mention; I found myself mildly aggravated by the all the sex. I’m no prude and I know Freud might disagree but I found it problematic that at times each characters’ key motivations, regrets and anxieties seemed sex-based. I’m not denying that humans are horny creatures but I like to cling to the ideal that not all men are ruled by their nobs at all times ... and that the average woman doesn’t have a rip-roaring orgasm at the drop of a hat (although, in fairness, the narrator does throw in a couple of failed female climaxes).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11315868270189164770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_64073142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64073142" />
    <a title="n* Dalal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/787126-n-dalal"><img alt="n* Dalal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201297014p2/787126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64073142?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="n* Dalal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="n* Dalal" href="/user/show/787126-n-dalal">n* Dalal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64073142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18292901121922679982">The Slap is about New Australia, an uncomfortable country of people living the direct contradiction between the white western world and an immigrant life; a fractured country where class, religion, and all those other big ideas break friendships and families apart.<br/><br/>But this book is also about the small things, the tiny lines people draw, the boundaries we fret over and keep us safe. Christos Tsiolkas explores the ideas that create generational difference. In a lot of ways, I intimately understand</span>
  <span id="freeText18292901121922679982" style="display:none">The Slap is about New Australia, an uncomfortable country of people living the direct contradiction between the white western world and an immigrant life; a fractured country where class, religion, and all those other big ideas break friendships and families apart.<br /><br />But this book is also about the small things, the tiny lines people draw, the boundaries we fret over and keep us safe. Christos Tsiolkas explores the ideas that create generational difference. In a lot of ways, I intimately understand what he's after. Where I draw my strength from, my mother can't fathom. When Aisha refuses to go to her brother-in-law's party, it's a matter of her personal principle. She won't go, she <i> can't </i> go. It would be going against her integrity. But, to her father-in-law, she is clearly just insulting the family. She is part of the family and her principles mean nothing against the monolithic idea of family. I know what that's like. When my cousin's marriage went south and it became clear that his and his parents' sexist swine behaviour led to his wife's suicide, I decided I would never talk to the bastard again. I thought surely he would be excommunicated from the family. <br /><br />But there he was, at the next wedding. Because he was family. It was a betrayal; not just to his late wife, but to every woman there. So, yeah, I know what Tsiolkas is talking about here.<br /><br />Another big theme is the idea of raising children in an ever more atomised society. Who is responsible for disciplining children? Their parents. But what happens when their parents don't discipline the children? And when those parents' parents are absent, nonexistent, not available to be proper grandparents? There is no one to tell the children they are wrong, no one to tell the child's parents that they are not doing their job. And who takes the responsibility? <br /><br />Tsiolkas raises important questions about the role of a community in raising a child...and the difficulty of being a parent without a community you trust.<br /><br />One of the issues I found most interesting was about the men. The book seems to be saying something about the diminishing role of men in the family. See, the story is told in several chapters, each from a different character's point of view. Aisha's husband Hector and his cousin Harry are two of three heterosexual men the book gets inside. Both Hector and Harry are married to beautiful women whom they love and respect. Both Hector and Harry are also cheating on their wives. Both Hector and Harry are ridiculously preoccupied with their penises; they jerk off several times a day; they jerk off to nineteen-year-old girls. It's a little pathetic. But in a way, it seems like these men feel that all the power they have left is in their virility. Aisha chooses not to go to a family party; it makes Hector look bad, his parents wish he'd married someone else, and he's insulted. And he can't do anything about it. Without the traditional, conservative roles of the family he grew up in, it's like all he has left are these pathetic gestures of faithlessness. And I think this i</span>
  <a data-text-id="18292901121922679982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192930398" />
    <a title="Dave" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5918722-dave"><img alt="Dave" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427395948p2/5918722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192930398?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dave" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dave" href="/user/show/5918722-dave">Dave</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781554686452" href="/book/show/6587397-the-slap">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192930398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer186270951685840275">The Good - An easy enough read with interesting topics of debate (whether it's appropriate to hit a child, fidelity, drugs), and a modern/diverse cast of characters. I read somewhere that it's like a long episode of neighbours,but souped with with lots of swearing... pretty accurate. <br/><br/><br/><br/>The Bad - The title of the book. The opening chapter - characters are introduced at a very fast pace so you've not a clue who is who. Language used isn't amazing, cliches, lots of pointless swearing (Too much use of</span>
  <span id="freeText186270951685840275" style="display:none">The Good - An easy enough read with interesting topics of debate (whether it's appropriate to hit a child, fidelity, drugs), and a modern/diverse cast of characters. I read somewhere that it's like a long episode of neighbours,but souped with with lots of swearing... pretty accurate. <br /><br /><br /><br />The Bad - The title of the book. The opening chapter - characters are introduced at a very fast pace so you've not a clue who is who. Language used isn't amazing, cliches, lots of pointless swearing (Too much use of the c word is not big or clever, especially on the first page). Despite the main topic of discussion, nothing is really discussed: "You should never hit a child", "But the child deserve it,", "But you should never a hit a child, FACT," , "But he deserved it, he is a brat," etc etc, repeat several times in each chapter. <br /><br /><br /><br />The Ugly - The "diverse" characters are all bloody horrible people at the extreme of stereotype. There's no subtlety to their feelings, actions, or dialogue, and even the ones I thought might be somewhere near normal turned out to be vapid monsters concerned only about image. It just isn't real life (not in my experience anyway) - it's very difficult to sympathise with any of them. Does everyone in Melbourne do drugs? Do they all hate their spouses? <br /><br /><br /><br />A lot of people will enjoy reading this (people who enjoy soaps) - and it is OK, but by Booker standards it would only get 1-2 rating. I find it funny that the author has slated the English novel too - this guy needs to a get a grip. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="186270951685840275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_125124245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125124245" />
    <a title="Spirited Stardust" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3316351-spirited-stardust"><img alt="Spirited Stardust" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476955975p2/3316351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125124245?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Spirited Stardust" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Spirited Stardust" href="/user/show/3316351-spirited-stardust">Spirited Stardust</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125124245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5080670881682361029">I had hoped a book as popular as this was popular because it was good - I was wrong.<br/>This novel places its merits on its characters, not on its writing or even its ability to tell a great story. I found none of its characters interesting or worthy to read about. Manolis was perhaps the only character I began to warm to, but as soon as I did, like every other character, a sordid, sexual deviancy was thrown in.<br/>And then there was the character of Richie, who was not only boring, but whose chapter in</span>
  <span id="freeText5080670881682361029" style="display:none">I had hoped a book as popular as this was popular because it was good - I was wrong.<br />This novel places its merits on its characters, not on its writing or even its ability to tell a great story. I found none of its characters interesting or worthy to read about. Manolis was perhaps the only character I began to warm to, but as soon as I did, like every other character, a sordid, sexual deviancy was thrown in.<br />And then there was the character of Richie, who was not only boring, but whose chapter in the book could have easily been thrown out and it wouldn't have mattered.<br /><br />Two thirds of the book is made up of drugs (I'm sorry but not every person of every age and every demographic takes drugs), sex and the description of male anatomy, the whole 'slap' incident was nothing more than a weak excuse to write chapters from every, boring character's view. I kept putting it down, and was unable to engrossed by it, and in all honesty, its vulgarity, lack of substance, and skill did not speak of 'braveness' nor 'brutal honesty' but rather of something completely common and uninspiring.<br /><br />A plucked sentence: This finally, was love. This was its shape and essence, once the lust and ecstasy and danger and adventure had gone. Love, at its core, was negotiation, the surrender of two individuals to the messy, banal, domestic realities of sharing a life together. Page 406.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5080670881682361029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_564379139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/564379139" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/187043-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184255514p2/187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/564379139?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/187043-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143117148" href="/book/show/6632916-the-slap">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/187043-laura?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/187043-laura?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer564379139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14769843505809411042">A man at a weekend barbecue slaps someone else's child in anger, and the act reverberates through his circle of friends and family. <br/><br/>I'm a bit mystified as to why this book has such a low rating here on Goodreads. But there were a couple of things I really admired about the book; uncoincidentally, those same theories might explain why some people seemed to dislike the book so much.<br/><br/>First of all, Tsiolkas takes a nonjudgmental attitude toward his characters. They not only do things we probably don'</span>
  <span id="freeText14769843505809411042" style="display:none">A man at a weekend barbecue slaps someone else's child in anger, and the act reverberates through his circle of friends and family. <br /><br />I'm a bit mystified as to why this book has such a low rating here on Goodreads. But there were a couple of things I really admired about the book; uncoincidentally, those same theories might explain why some people seemed to dislike the book so much.<br /><br />First of all, Tsiolkas takes a nonjudgmental attitude toward his characters. They not only do things we probably don't admire much, but they do some genuinely awful things, too. Yet nothing terrible happens to them; they go about their lives without getting the karmic slap with a two-by-four that a lot of readers not only want but have come to expect (<i>see e.g. East of Eden</i>). I suspect this drives that same group of readers completely nuts.<br /><br />What I suspect angered readers even more is the one character that people seem to despise without even quite realizing what's creating such violently negative reaction: the mother who not only doesn't wax rhapsodic with every breath about how motherhood is the best thing she's ever done, but actually detests motherhood and probably detests her child, too. This book contains that character and then some in Rosie, the mother of the child receiving the slap. (Check the reviews on Charlotte Mendelsohn's "When We Were Bad"; another book that got horrible ratings that you can't quite figure out -- similar character, same explanation. Although that book also wasn't helped by the fact that a couple of people seemed to also go insane at its use of Yiddish and Hebrew words. A totally different subject that I won't talk about or <i>I'll</i> go insane.) Rosie hates being a mother and also hates her kid, a vile little brat who is eminently hatable (unsurprisingly, given the rotten parent hand that life dealt the little shit). <br /><br />But again, Tsiolkas doesn't condemn Rosie, nor does he paint her as a monster or make her see the error of her ways by the last page. She continues on unchanged, and Tsiolkas gives the impression that she'll do so long after the book has ended. He also very much takes his time in revealing her character -- another thing I admired about the book.<br /><br />To me, these things make the book nuanced; to a lot of readers, I guess, they make the book immoral.<br /><br />I would probably normally give this one four stars instead of five, but the rating is so shamefully low that I bumped up my own in the benighted hope that the overall rating would tick up slightly. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14769843505809411042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115907904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115907904" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3269646-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469570174p2/3269646.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115907904?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/3269646-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848873551" href="/book/show/7743874-the-slap">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3269646-amanda?shelf=bought-copy">bought-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3269646-amanda?shelf=literary">literary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115907904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2487178850335023235">The Slap is a novel looking at a cross section of Australian life by taking the viewpoints of eight characters, all whom were present at the BBQ where the eponymous slap took place. Hector is first up, a Greek bureaucrat, married to Indian Aisha but considering an affair; then Anouk, a hard Jewish writer who cannot see the problem with hitting a child - and, in general, has no understanding of, or liking for, children; Harry is next - Hector's hot-headed cousin who delivered the slap. Connie is </span>
  <span id="freeText2487178850335023235" style="display:none">The Slap is a novel looking at a cross section of Australian life by taking the viewpoints of eight characters, all whom were present at the BBQ where the eponymous slap took place. Hector is first up, a Greek bureaucrat, married to Indian Aisha but considering an affair; then Anouk, a hard Jewish writer who cannot see the problem with hitting a child - and, in general, has no understanding of, or liking for, children; Harry is next - Hector's hot-headed cousin who delivered the slap. Connie is a teenager who regularly looks after Hugo, the child who was slapped, and dreams of becoming a vet; Rosie is the mother of Hugo, pathologically attached to him and still breast feeding her child even though he is three years old; Manolis is the father of Hector, a doting grandfather and fiercely Greek. Finally we hear from Aisha herself, as she and Hector take a holiday where truths come out, and Richie, Connie's best friend, a young lad waiting to hear his exam results and struggling with the fact he is gay.<br /><br />I struggled with this book. It is annoyingly readable, but has so many flaws that, despite a storming and compelling start, it really tails off towards the end of the novel and you find yourself wondering why you are still reading.<br /><br />The premise is fantastic - taking a child being slapped as a starting point, and exploring how this affects friends and family is just brilliant. I heard about this book at a blogger event and was determined to seek it out and read it purely based on the premise. It must be such a great sell - in fact, I have mentioned it to other people and they have shown the same intrigue.<br /><br />Tsiolkas does a brilliant job at showing us a cross section of Australian life, a seething mass of religions and cultures, sexualities and races. With this morass of humanity, conflict is inevitable and Tsiolkas handles the macro issues of life in Australia as well as the micro.<br /><br />I also liked how Tsiolkas was able to explore perceptions of people through the slap - at first we think Harry possibly had a case for slapping a child who was both misbehaving and threatening his own child (as much as anyone has a case for slapping a child, anyway), but then we discover that Harry is a foul-tempered man who keeps a mistress and has hit his wife in the past. I enjoyed having my perceptions overthrown like this - a literal exploration of not judging someone by first impressions.<br /><br />So that is the good... On to the bad...<br /><br />I've mentioned my dislike of profanity in books before. I can handle it when it feels natural and when it serves the plot - here we had (excuse me) cocks and cunts on virtually every page. It was an endless stream of bad language - and mostly used in universally poor sex scenes. It got to the point where I was sickened by the profanity and the relentless, grotesque mentions of masturbation and rough sex.<br /><br />In fact, this book hit a number of my literary black spots: women being mistreated in terms of hitting them and forcing them into sex; young girls feeling as though they have to have sex to make them women; adultery; flagrant and accepted use of hard drugs. This book was simply filled with horrible misogynist men and women with victim complexes.<br /><br />The pacing of the novel was entirely off. The premise was to do with the slap and this drove the narrative admirably for the first two thirds. The resolution to this part of the tale came way too early, and left me wondering why I was still reading the novel as it petered off into a limp ending.<br /><br />Also, for a literary novel, this felt very much like a trashy summer read. I could imagine seeing similar characters and events in a novel that is as far from Booker Prize winning as I can imagine!<br /><br />Altogether, I hated this book. Yet I read it greedily and compulsively. Something must have driven me to keep turning these pages, and I guess it was Tsiolkas' writing. Ultimately I wanted to finish the novel - whether that was simply wanting to find out the result of the court case, or seeing whether Tsiolkas could descent into worse depths of depravity in his writing.<br /><br />Man Booker thoughts: Please don't let this book win! It might have something to say on racism, homosexuality, the life of ordinary people, but it is wrapped up in a novel that is filled with one dimensional cliched characters. There must be better novels on the long list than this one... </span>
  <a data-text-id="2487178850335023235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1771591388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1771591388" />
    <a title="Sharon Robards" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9624255-sharon-robards"><img alt="Sharon Robards" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460850161p2/9624255.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1771591388?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Robards" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Robards" href="/user/show/9624255-sharon-robards">Sharon Robards</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9624255-sharon-robards?shelf=australian-authors">australian-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9624255-sharon-robards?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1771591388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8592015455408187786">Why no rating? <br/><br/>This is the type of book which makes me greatly dislike the rating system. In my opinion it isn’t the worst of books nor the best of books. But, I almost didn’t get past the first chapter, and then found myself skiming here and there from the third or fourth chapter. Each of the 8 chapters were told from a different POV, so a rating seems a little unfair as perhaps I missed some defining moment in what at times seemed to be much to do about nothing, but an injection of a lot backs</span>
  <span id="freeText8592015455408187786" style="display:none">Why no rating? <br /><br />This is the type of book which makes me greatly dislike the rating system. In my opinion it isn’t the worst of books nor the best of books. But, I almost didn’t get past the first chapter, and then found myself skiming here and there from the third or fourth chapter. Each of the 8 chapters were told from a different POV, so a rating seems a little unfair as perhaps I missed some defining moment in what at times seemed to be much to do about nothing, but an injection of a lot backstory. <br /><br />I don’t really understand what all the fuss was about it, but can see why the movie makers wanted to jump onto the band wagon. Almost not a page where someone isn’t either having sex or thinking about it, unfaithful husbands and wives, illect drugs, a multicultural cast of characters, from two male Greek cousins, their wives, one of Indian heritage and the other Australian, an aboroginal man converted to Islam, two Australian teenagagers, an Australian couple, and one of the Greek fellows parents, plus a few others thrown into the plot. <br /><br />Everyone knows what the plot is supposed to be about. A man who slaps another persons child at a barbeque and the consenquences from that incident. I found the book greatly character driven, but had trouble with almost all of the charchters motivations and their reactions to incidents and each other. It was almost like to me that they were all slapped onto the page and there was no control or deep thought into what motivates people deeply — BEYOND SEX. <br /><br />I’m not sure if I have over thought it too much while reading or those who loved the book did. It probably didn’t serve me well that this is the second book I’ve read in a row where the plot device to surprise readers appears to inject an unfaithful husband or wife or both, and oh, shock, a middle aged man with the hots for teenage girl, which I found boring. <br /><br />A review fromt the Canberra Times said in part, “And it can radically alter your view of the world.” <br /><br />If I took away anything from the book it would be two things … one … this is Christos Tsiolkas view of his world, certainly not mine, but perhaps there is some honesty in each character that might reflect a little of our own or partner’s hidden and inner selves and that I don't need fiction to tell me that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8592015455408187786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HTdQa3gZzfWp24s2KSaYUDdZJa4JDFbl7qQuQCwg/z0Twz2jIvl5/bCpdBigOKix5HLFCQDFGE3Yad3xLbCvBQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QXfac5S2IWNb4n8w1VurRwTfZ2VrC9KhoVw5k4f9eMdPg7e7zlaVa0KQgB5cRZum1/SHwmLCnAmXkcoihm0o/w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

An award-winning work, Cloudstreet e<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText38133569088904123\" style=\"display:none\">Hailed as a classic, Tim Winton\'s masterful family saga is both a paean to working-class Australians and an unflinching examination of the human heart\'s capacity for sorrow, joy, and endless gradations in between. An award-winning work, Cloudstreet exemplifies the brilliant ability of fiction to captivate and inspire.  Struggling to rebuild their lives after being touched by disaster, the Pickle family, who\'ve inherited a big house called Cloudstreet in a suburb of Perth, take in the God-fearing Lambs as tenants. The Lambs have suffered their own catastrophes, and determined to survive, they open up a grocery on the ground floor. From 1944 to 1964, the shared experiences of the two overpopulated clans -- running the gamut from drunkenness, adultery, and death to resurrection, marriage, and birth -- bond them to each other and Neither of them would call it love, but they can\'t stay away from each other no matter how dangerous it is, and out on White Point it is very dangerous.  Set in the dramatic landscape of Western Australia, Dirt Music is a love story about people stifled by grief and regret; a novel about the odds of breaking with the past and about the lure of music. Dirt music, Fox tells Georgie, is &quot;anything you can play on a verandah or porch, without electricity.&quot; Even in the wild, Luther cannot escape it. There is, he discovers, no silence in nature.  Ambitious, perfectly calibrated, Dirt Music resonates with suspense and supercharged emotion, and it confirms Tim Winton\'s status as the preeminent Australian novelist of his generation.<\/span>\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/61015.Christos_Tsiolkas">About Christos Tsiolkas</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/61015.Christos_Tsiolkas"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1313611980p3/61015.jpg);'></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7100131895315758583">Christos Tsiolkas is the author of nine novels: <i>Loaded</i>, which was made into the feature film Head-On, <i>The Jesus Man</i> and <i>Dead Europe</i>,which won the 2006 Age Fiction Prize and the 2006 Melbourne Best Writing Award. He won Overall Best Book in the Commonwealth Writers' Prize 2009, was shortlisted for the 2009 Miles Franklin Literary Award, long listed for the 2010 Man Booker Prize and won the Australi</span>
  <span id="freeText7100131895315758583" style="display:none">Christos Tsiolkas is the author of nine novels: <i>Loaded</i>, which was made into the feature film Head-On, <i>The Jesus Man</i> and <i>Dead Europe</i>,which won the 2006 Age Fiction Prize and the 2006 Melbourne Best Writing Award. He won Overall Best Book in the Commonwealth Writers' Prize 2009, was shortlisted for the 2009 Miles Franklin Literary Award, long listed for the 2010 Man Booker Prize and won the Australian Literary Society Gold Medal for <i>The Slap</i>, which was also announced as the 2009 Australian Booksellers Association and Australian Book Industry Awards Books of the Year. <br /><i>Barracuda</i> is his fifth novel. <i>Merciless Gods</i> (2014) and <i>Damascus</i> (2019) followed.<br />He is also a playwright, essayist and screen writer. He lives in Melbourne.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7100131895315758583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
